7:01:58 So first of all,
7:01:59 what exactly is cross-site scripting?
7:02:01 Well cross-site scripting
7:02:03 refers to client-side code injection attacks
7:02:05 where in an attacker
7:02:07 can execute a malicious script also commonly referred
7:02:10 to as a malicious payload into a legitimate website
7:02:14 or web application now xss is amongst the most rampant
7:02:17 of web application vulnerabilities and occurs
7:02:20 when of Web application makes use of something
7:02:23 like a nun validated
7:02:24 or unencoded user input within the output
7:02:26 that it generates Now by leveraging xss
7:02:30 and attacker does not Target a victim directly instead
7:02:34 an attacker would be exploiting a vulnerability within a website
7:02:37 or something like a web application
7:02:39 that the victim would visit
7:02:41 and essentially using the vulnerable website
7:02:43 or the web application as a vehicle to deliver
7:02:46 a malicious script to the victims browser.
7:02:49 Now while exercise can be taken advantage
7:02:52 of within a virtual box script ActiveX and Flash
7:02:56 unquestionably the most widely abused is Javascript.
7:02:59 This is mostly
7:03:00 because JavaScript is the fundamental
7:03:02 to any browsing experience all
7:03:04 the modern sides today have some JavaScript framework running
7:03:07 in the background now xss can be used
7:03:11 in a range of ways to cause serious problems.
7:03:14 Well, the traditional is uses of exercise is the ability
7:03:17 for an attacker to steal.
7:03:18 Session cookies allowing
7:03:20 an attacker to probably impersonate a victim and
7:03:22 that Justin's and that just doesn't stop there.

7:03:28 on social websites spread
7:03:29 malware website defa commence and fish for credentials
7:03:32 and even used in conjunction
7:03:34 with some clever social engineering techniques
7:03:36 to escalate to even more damaging attacks.
7:03:40 Now cross site scripting can be classified
7:03:42 into three major categories.
7:03:44 So the first is reflected cross-site scripting.
7:03:47 The second is stored or persistent cross-site scripting
7:03:50 and the third is dom-based cross-site scripting so
7:03:52 out here Dom refers to the document object model
7:03:55 that is used file web application building.
7:03:58 So let's take a moment to discuss the three types
7:04:01 of cross-site scripting.
7:04:02 So the first one we're going to be discussing is reflected
7:04:05 cross-site scripting Now
7:04:07 by far the most common type of cross-site scripting
7:04:09 that you'll become.
7:04:10 Because is probably reflected cross-site scripting here.
7:04:13 The attackers payload
7:04:14 is a script and has to be part of a request
7:04:17 which is sent to the web server and reflected back in such a way
7:04:20 that the HTTP response includes the payload
7:04:23 from the HTTP request Now using a phishing email
7:04:27 and other social engineering techniques the attacker layers
7:04:30 in the victim to inadvertently make a request to the server
7:04:33 which contains the cross site scripting payload,
7:04:36 and then he ends up executing the script
7:04:38 that gets reflected and cute it inside his own browser.
7:04:42 Now since reflected cross-site scripting isn't really
7:04:44 a persistent kind
7:04:45 of attack the attacker needs to deliver
7:04:47 this payload to each victim
7:04:49 that he wants to serve.
7:04:50 So a medium like a social network is very conveniently
7:04:53 used for destination of these attacks.
7:04:55 So now let's take a step by step.
7:04:57 Look at how cross-site scripting actually works.
7:05:00 So firstly the attacker crafts a URL containing
7:05:03 a malicious string and sends it to the victim.
7:05:07 Now the poor victim is tricked by the attacker
7:05:09 into requesting the URL from the website,
7:05:11 which is running a I respond script
7:05:13 and then the website includes the militia string
7:05:16 from the URL in the response.
7:05:17 And then in the end the victims browser executes,
7:05:20 the malicious script inside the response sending
7:05:22 the victims cookies to the attacker silver.
7:05:25 Okay.
7:05:26 So at first reflected xss might seem very harmless
7:05:29 because it requires a victim himself to actually send
7:05:32 a request containing a militia string now
7:05:35 since nobody would be willingly attacking himself.
7:05:37 So there seems to be
7:05:38 no way of actually performing the attack but
7:05:41 as it turns out there are at least two common ways
7:05:44 of causing a victim
7:05:45 to launcher reflected cross-eyed attack on himself.
7:05:48 So the first way is
7:05:49 if the user or targets a specific individual
7:05:51 and the attacker can send the malicious URL to the victim.
7:05:55 For example using email or for example instant messaging
7:05:59 and then trick him into visiting the site.
7:06:02 Secondly if the user targets a large group
7:06:04 of people the attacker then can publish the link
7:06:07 or the malicious URL
7:06:08 or his own website or social media,
7:06:10 and then he'll just wait for visitors to click on it.
7:06:14 So these two methods are similar
7:06:16 and both can be very successful with the use
7:06:19 of a URL shortening service like one provided by Google.
7:06:22 So this masks the militia string from users
7:06:24 who might otherwise identifier.
7:06:27 Okay.
7:06:27 So that was all about reflected cross-site scripting.
7:06:30 Let's move on to store cross-site scripting now.
7:06:33 So the most damaging type of cross-site scripting
7:06:36 that is there today is persistent or stored
7:06:38 cross-site scripting installed cross-site scripting attacks.
7:06:42 It attacks.
7:06:43 I'm sorry installed cross-site scripting attacks.
7:06:46 The attacker is injecting a script into the database
7:06:49 that is permanently stored on the target application.

7:06:53 is a malicious script inserted by an attacker

7:07:00 to the affected webpage now in a browser
7:07:03 The cross site scripting payload will be served.
7:07:05 As a part of the web page just
7:07:07 like any legitimate comment would be now.
7:07:09 This means that the victim will be inadvertently ended
7:07:11 up ending up executing the malicious script.
7:07:14 Once the page is viewed in the browser.
7:07:16 Now, let's also take a step by step.
7:07:18 Look at how cross-site scripting in the stored version works.
7:07:21 So the attacker uses one of the websites form to insert
7:07:24 a malicious string into the websites database first.
7:07:27 Now the victim unknowingly request the page
7:07:30 from the website
7:07:31 and then the website Glued some malicious string
7:07:34 from the database in the response
7:07:35 and then sends it to the victim.
7:07:37 Now the poor victim will be actually executing
7:07:40 the malicious script inside the response
7:07:42 and sending all the cookies to the attackers server.
7:07:45 So that's basically
7:07:46 how stored or persistent cross-site scripting works.
7:07:50 Now it's time for the last type of cross-site scripting
7:07:54 which is document object model based cross-site scripting.
7:07:57 So dom-based cross-site scripting is an advanced type
7:08:00 of cross-site scripting attack.
7:08:02 So which is made possible
7:08:04 when the web applications client-side script writer uses
7:08:08 provided data to the document object model.
7:08:11 So basically it means
7:08:12 that data is subsequently read from the document object model

7:27:32 which request rendering
7:27:33 them unusable the dying Wireless authentication
7:27:36 and eyeing any sort of service
7:27:38 that is provided on the internet attacks
7:27:40 of such intent can be performed from a single machine
7:27:43 while single machine attacks are much easier to execute
7:27:45 and monitor their also easy
7:27:47 to detect and mitigate to solve this issue.
7:27:49 The attack could be executed from multiple devices spread
7:27:52 across a wide area.
7:27:54 Not only does this make it difficult to stop the attack
7:27:57 but it also becomes near impossible to point out.
7:27:59 The main culprit such attacks are called distributed denial
7:28:02 of service or DDOS attacks.

7:28:08 Attack as explained
7:28:09 is making a certain service unavailable since everything
7:28:12 that is attacked is in reality running on a machine.
7:28:15 The service can be made available.
7:28:17 If the performance of the machine can be brought down.

7:29:19 of death attack exploits this particular fact
7:29:22 in this type of attack.

7:29:32 or sometimes crashing entirely then we come
7:29:34 to reflect on the docks this particular attack.
7:29:37 Iraq is more often than not used with the help of a botnet.

7:29:42 of innocent computers a connection request

7:29:49 like it comes from the victim and this is done

7:29:56 an acknowledgement to the victim computer

7:30:01 to the same machine this overloads the computer

7:30:36 the starting position or offset.
